Now let me check each candidate for whether it can produce exactly these four basis functions.

### Candidate 1:
`T*c0*epsilon**4/(c1 + epsilon) + c2*epsilon*exp(c3*epsilon) + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon + c7`

The first term: `T*epsilon**4/(c1+epsilon)`. If c1=0, this becomes `T*epsilon**3`. The exp term can't be eliminated to give epsilon**3 unless c3=0, giving `c2*epsilon`. With c5=3, we get `c4*epsilon**3`. So: T*epsilon**3 + c2*epsilon + c4*epsilon**3 + c6*epsilon + c7. This gives T*epsilon**3, epsilon**3, epsilon, 1. But GT needs a standalone T term. **No T term available.**

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 2:
All terms have factor `1/(c2+epsilon)`. If c2=0, all terms become divided by epsilon. Let me check with c2=0:
`T*c0*epsilon*epsilon**c1/epsilon + T*c3*epsilon**c1/epsilon + c4/epsilon + c5*log(c6*epsilon+1)/epsilon + c7 + c8*log(c6*epsilon+1) + c9`

With c1=3: `T*c0*epsilon**3 + T*c3*epsilon**2 + c4/epsilon + ...` - has log terms and 1/epsilon that can't be eliminated cleanly. Setting c5=0, c8=0, c6→0: still have c4/epsilon. Set c4=0: `T*c0*epsilon**3 + T*c3*epsilon**2 + (c7+c9) + 0`. This gives T*epsilon**3, T*epsilon**2, 1. Missing standalone T and epsilon**3.

Can't match.

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 3:
`T*c0*epsilon**c1/(c2 + epsilon) + c3*epsilon*exp(c4*epsilon) + c5*epsilon**c6 + c7*epsilon + c8`

With c2=0: `T*c0*epsilon**(c1-1)`. Set c1=4: `T*c0*epsilon**3`. Set c4=0: `c3*epsilon`. Set c6=3: `c5*epsilon**3`. Total: `T*c0*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon + c5*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon + c8`. Missing standalone T term.

Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 4:
`T*c0*epsilon**4/(c1+epsilon) + T**c2*c3*epsilon**2/(c1+epsilon) + T**c2*c4*epsilon**3/(c1+epsilon) + c5/(c1+epsilon) + c6*exp(c7*epsilon)/(c1+epsilon) + c8*epsilon/(c1+epsilon) + c9*epsilon*exp(c7*epsilon)/(c1+epsilon)`

Set c1=0: all terms lose the denominator (divided by epsilon).
`T*c0*epsilon**3 + T**c2*c3*epsilon + T**c2*c4*epsilon**2 + c5/epsilon + c6*exp(c7*epsilon)/epsilon + c8 + c9*exp(c7*epsilon)`

This is messy. Set c5=0, c7=0: `T*c0*epsilon**3 + T**c2*c3*epsilon + T**c2*c4*epsilon**2 + c6/epsilon + c8 + c9`. Still have 1/epsilon. Can't work cleanly.

Let me try differently. Keep c1 general. The common denominator is (c1+epsilon). For GT, we need:
`(c1+epsilon) * [8.638*T*epsilon**3 - 0.3903*T - 2663.88*epsilon**3 + 120.55]`

This would expand to terms with T*epsilon**4, T*epsilon**3, T*epsilon, T, epsilon**4, epsilon**3, epsilon, 1.

The candidate (multiplied by (c1+epsilon)) gives:
`T*c0*epsilon**4 + T**c2*c3*epsilon**2 + T**c2*c4*epsilon**3 + c5 + c6*exp(c7*epsilon) + c8*epsilon + c9*epsilon*exp(c7*epsilon)`

For T**c2 to give T, set c2=1. Set c7=0: exp terms become constants.
`T*c0*epsilon**4 + T*c3*epsilon**2 + T*c4*epsilon**3 + c5 + c6 + c8*epsilon + c9*epsilon`

This gives: T*epsilon**4, T*epsilon**2, T*epsilon**3, 1, epsilon. But GT*(c1+epsilon) needs T*epsilon**4, T*epsilon**3, T*epsilon, T, epsilon**4, epsilon**3, epsilon, 1.

Missing T*epsilon (need T*epsilon from GT), missing T, missing epsilon**4, missing epsilon**3. Has T*epsilon**2 which shouldn't be there. Can't match.

Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 5:
All terms over (c2+epsilon). Set c2=0:
`T*c0*epsilon**c1 + T*c3*epsilon**(c1-1) + c4/epsilon + (c5+c6+c7) + c8*epsilon`

Set c1=3: `T*c0*epsilon**3 + T*c3*epsilon**2 + c4/epsilon + const + c8*epsilon`. Has T*epsilon**2 and 1/epsilon. Set c3=0, c4=0: `T*c0*epsilon**3 + const + c8*epsilon`. Missing T and epsilon**3.

Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 6:
All over (c1+epsilon). Set c1=0:
`T*c0*epsilon**3 + T*c2*epsilon**2 + c3/epsilon + (c4+c5+c6) + c7*epsilon`

Set c2=0, c3=0: `T*c0*epsilon**3 + const + c7*epsilon`. Missing T and epsilon**3.

Alternatively, keep c1 nonzero. Multiply both sides by (c1+epsilon):
GT*(c1+epsilon) = 8.638*T*epsilon**3*(c1+epsilon) - 0.3903*T*(c1+epsilon) - 2663.88*epsilon**3*(c1+epsilon) + 120.55*(c1+epsilon)
= 8.638*c1*T*epsilon**3 + 8.638*T*epsilon**4 - 0.3903*c1*T - 0.3903*T*epsilon - 2663.88*c1*epsilon**3 - 2663.88*epsilon**4 + 120.55*c1 + 120.55*epsilon

Candidate 6 * (c1+epsilon):
`T*c0*epsilon**4 + T*c2*epsilon**3 + c3 + (c4+c5+c6)*epsilon + c7*epsilon**2`

Comparing: Need T*epsilon**4 ✓(c0), T*epsilon**3 ✓(c2), T ✗(missing), T*epsilon ✗(missing), epsilon**4 ✗(missing), epsilon**3 ✗(missing), 1 ✓(c3), epsilon ✓, epsilon**2 ✗(extra).

Missing too many terms.

Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 7:
This has (c4+epsilon)**3 terms and exp(T*c7) terms. The exp(T*c7) introduces exponential dependence on T which GT doesn't have (unless c7=0). Set c7=0: exp terms become constants.

All over (c1+epsilon). Multiply by (c1+epsilon):
`T*c0*epsilon**4 + T*c2*epsilon**3 + T*c3*(c4+epsilon)**3 + T*c5*epsilon*(c4+epsilon)**3 + c6 + c8*epsilon + c9*epsilon`

Expand (c4+epsilon)**3 = c4**3 + 3*c4**2*epsilon + 3*c4*epsilon**2 + epsilon**3.

T*c3*(c4+epsilon)**3 gives T*(c3*c4**3 + 3*c3*c4**2*epsilon + 3*c3*c4*epsilon**2 + c3*epsilon**3)
T*c5*epsilon*(c4+epsilon)**3 gives T*(c5*c4**3*epsilon + 3*c5*c4**2*epsilon**2 + 3*c5*c4*epsilon**3 + c5*epsilon**4)

Total T-dependent terms: T*c0*epsilon**4 + T*c2*epsilon**3 + T*c3*c4**3 + T*(3*c3*c4**2)*epsilon + T*(3*c3*c4)*epsilon**2 + T*c3*epsilon**3 + T*c5*c4**3*epsilon + T*(3*c5*c4**2)*epsilon**2 + T*(3*c5*c4)*epsilon**3 + T*c5*epsilon**4

GT*(c1+epsilon) T-terms: 8.638*c1*T*epsilon**3 + 8.638*T*epsilon**4 - 0.3903*c1*T - 0.3903*T*epsilon

We need T*epsilon**2 coefficient = 0: 3*c3*c4 + 3*c5*c4**2 = 0 → c3 = -c5*c4.
We need T*epsilon**4: c0 + c5 = 8.638
T*epsilon**3: c2 + c3 + 3*c5*c4 = 8.638*c1 → c2 - c5*c4 + 3*c5*c4 = c2 + 2*c5*c4 = 8.638*c1
T*epsilon: 3*c3*c4**2 + c5*c4**3 = -0.3903 → 3*(-c5*c4)*c4**2 + c5*c4**3 = -3*c5*c4**3 + c5*c4**3 = -2*c5*c4**3 = -0.3903
T: c3*c4**3 = -0.3903*c1 → -c5*c4**4 = -0.3903*c1

Non-T terms: c6 + (c8+c9)*epsilon. GT needs: -2663.88*c1*epsilon**3 - 2663.88*epsilon**4 + 120.55*c1 + 120.55*epsilon.

But non-T terms only have constant and epsilon. Missing epsilon**3 and epsilon**4. Can't match.

Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 8:
All over (c1+epsilon). Multiply by (c1+epsilon):

### Candidate 11:

With c1≠0, we get T*epsilon**3, T*epsilon**2, T*epsilon, T from the cubic. We can use c3 to cancel T*epsilon and c2 to adjust T. But T*epsilon**2 = 3*c0*c1 can only be zero if c1=0. And with c1=0, no epsilon**3 non-T term.
